1 Scope 1 
The present document specifies the O1 Interface specification for O -DU used over the interface linking the O-DU (O-2 
RAN Distributed Unit) with other management plane entities, that may include the O-CU (O-RAN Central Unit) as well 3 
as Service Management and Orchestration (SMO).  4 
2 References 5 
2.1 Normative references 6 
References are either specific (identified by date of publication, edition numbe r, version number, etc.) or non -specific. 7 
For a specific reference, subsequent revisions do not apply. For a non-specific reference, the latest version applies. In the 8 
case of a reference to a 3GPP document (including a GSM docume nt), a non -specific reference implicitly refers to the 9 
latest version of that document in Release 17. 10

3 Definitions of terms, symbols and abbreviations 22 
3.1 Terms 23 
For the purposes of the present document, the terms and definitions given in 3GPP TR 21.905 [1] and the following apply. 24 
A term define d in the present document takes precedence over the definition of the same term, if any, in 3GPP 25 
TR 21.905 [1]. 26 
Advanced Sleep Mode (ASM): Advanced sleep mode may be used to achieve energy saving by disabling some fraction 27 
of the O-RU’s processing for a defined or undefined period of time. 28 
Antenna Line: connection between O-RU and antenna 29 
C-Plane: Control Plane: refers specifically to real -time control between O-DU and O-RU, and should not be confused 30 
with the UE’s control plane 31 
c_eAxC: component eAxC: a portion of an eAxC flow assigned to a specific O-DU processing element.  32 
DL: Downlink: data flow towards the radiating antenna (generally on the LLS interface) 33 
DU: Distributed Unit: a logical node hosting RLC/MAC/High-PHY/Low-PHY layers and RF processing layers based on 34 
a higher layer functional split for integrated model 35 
eAxC: extended Antenna-Carrier: a data flow for a single antenna (or spatial stream) for a single carrier in a single sector. 36 
Emergency Wake-up: In TRX Control and Advanced Sleep Mode energy saving techniques, the CU -Plane processing 37 
unit of O -RU may be turned off, hence O -DU can’t wake -up the O -RU from sleep through C -Plane. When C -Plane is 38 
disabled, M-Plane shall be used to abort the ongoing Advanced Sleep Modes and TRX Control. 39 
Energy Saving Policy: A set of rules and conditions defined by the MnS Consumer that, when provided to O -DU, shall 40 
be used by O -DU to decide when and for how long to utilize specific type of Energy Savin g. As such, Energy Saving 41 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        12 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 Policy is not exact command that triggers addressee to immediately apply specific Advanced Sleep Mode or to activate / 1 
deactivate cells / carriers. 2 
Note: It is not prohibited for single policy to contain rules and conditionals for  more than one Energy Saving Mode. 3 
FFT/iFFT: Fast Fourier Transform/inverse Fast Fourier Transform: an algorithm that computes discrete Fourier 4 
transform or its inverse. 5 
High-PHY: those portions of the PHY processing on the O-DU side of the  fronthaul interface, including FEC 6 
encode/decode, scrambling, and modulation/demodulation. 7 
IOC: Information Object Class. 8 
LLS: Lower Layer Split: logical interface between  O-DU and O-RU when using a  lower layer ( intra-PHY based ) 9 
functional split. 10 
LLS-C: Lower Layer Split Control-plane: logical interface between O-DU and O-RU when using a lower layer functional 11 
split. 12 
Low-PHY: those portions of the PHY processing on the O-RU side of the fronthaul interface, including FFT/iFFT, digital 13 
beamforming, and PRACH extraction and filtering. 14 
M-Plane: Management Plane: refers to non-real-time management operations between the O-DU and the O-RU 15 
MnS Consumer: The Network Element that consumes and utilizes Management Services (here SMO or non -RT RIC). 16 
MnS Producer: The Network Element that produces Management Services (here O-DU or O-CU). 17 
Multi O-DU O-RU: An O-RU that supports the SHARED-ORU-MULTI-ODU feature  18 
Multi-Operator O-RU: An O-RU that supports the SHARED-ORU-MULTI-OPERATOR and SHARED-ORU-19 
MULTI-ODU features 20 
O-CU: O-RAN Central Unit: a logical node hosting in the Control Plane (O-CU-CP) the RRC and the Control Plane part 21 
of the PDCP protocol and in the User Plane (O-CU-UP) the user plane part of the PDCP protocol and the SDAP protocol. 22 
O-CU-CP: O-RAN Central Unit: Control Plane: a logical node hosting the RRC and the control plane part of the PDCP 23 
protocol. 24 
O-CU-UP: O-RAN Central Unit: User Plane: a logical node hosting the user plane part of the PDCP protocol and the 25 
SDAP protocol. 26 
O-DU: O-RAN Distributed Unit — A logical node hosting RLC/MAC/High-PHY layers based on a lower layer functional 27 
split. 28 
O-RU: O-RAN Radio Unit: a logical node hosting Low-PHY layer and RF processing based on a higher layer functional 29 
split in 3-box model.  This is similar to 3GPP’s “TRP” or “RRH” but more specific in including the Low -PHY layer 30 
(FFT/iFFT, PRACH extraction).   31 
Port: End of a transport link – in most cases this is an optical port 32 
Port Number: A number which identifies a port (see Port). In c ase of SFP/SFP+ port, port number value is 0 to N -1 33 
where N is number of ports in the device. Numbers 0 to N -1 are assigned to ports in order following order of labels on 34 
the device (labels for ports are not necessarily numbers starting from zero) 35 
S-Plane: Synchronization Plane: refers to traffic between the O-RU or O-DU to a synchronization controller which is 36 
generally an IEEE-1588 Grand Master (however, Grand Master functionality may be embedded in the O-DU). 37 
Shared O-RU Host: The role performed by the NETCONF client associated with the operator of a Multi-Operator O-38 
RU who determines how the resources of a Multi-Operator O-RU are partitioned between Shared Resource Operators. 39 
Shared O-RU Host O-DU: The O-DU performing Shared O-RU Host role. 40 
Shared Resource Operator: The role performed by the NETCONF client associated with an operator that utilizes the 41 
carrier resources of a Multi -Operator O -RU. The Shared Resource Operator is allocated a Shared Resource Operator 42 
identity by the Shared O-RU Host. 43 
NOTE: A NETCONF client of an operator can simultaneously perform the Shared O-RU Host role and the Shared 44 
Resource Operator role. Alternatively, a NETCONF client of an operator can only perform the Shared O -RU Host 45 
role and not Shared Resource Operator role, in which case the operator corresponds to a neutral host operator. 46 
Shared Resource Operator O-DU: The O-DU performing Shared Resource Operator role. 47 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        13 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 Spatial stream: the data flow on the DL associated with precoded data (may be same as layers or different if the re is 1 
expansion in the precoding), and on UL associated with the number of outputs from the digital beamforming (sometimes 2 
called “beams”).  3 
SSM: Synchronization Status Message: part of ITU G.781 and G.8264 standards. 4 
TRX Control: TRX control may be used t o achieve energy saving through disabling one or more O -RU antenna array 5 
elements for a defined or undefined period of time. 6 
U-Plane: User Plane: refers to IQ sample data between O-DU and O-RU. 7 
UL: Uplink: data flow away from the radiating antenna (generally on the LLS interface) 8

3.4 Conventions 25 
This management plane specification includes cross references to a set of associated YANG models. Text may reference 26 
particular YANG leafs, notifications and remote procedure calls (RPCs). In order to assist in readability, all cross 27 
references to YANG defined elements will keep the identical case format as defined in the corresponding YANG model, 28 
with the font-weight set to bold. This convention applies only to text and not to YANG elements embedded into figures.   29 
If there is any conflict between the YANG models and the accompanying text description in this specification, the 30 
definition of the YANG models shall take precedence. 31 
 32 
3.5 Revision and compatibility handling 33 
The revision statement in the YANG models shall be used to describe future revisions to the mo dels that are backwards 34 
compatible. Backwards incompatible changes will be addressed by incrementing the number used as part of the model 35 
name and namespace, effectively creating a new YANG model. The format of the namespace used in all O-RAN YANG 36 
models is “urn:o-ran:”<model-name>“:”<model-number>, where the initial <model -number> used in a newly defined 37 
YANG model is “1.0”. Where this document makes reference to models, irre spective of their backward compatibility, a 38 
generic <model-number> of “x.y” is used to enable reference to all versions of the namespace for a particular <model -39 
name>. 40 
 41 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        15 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 The revision statement in all YANG models includes a reference statement used to cross -reference to the first version of 1 
this document where the corresponding description was introduced. For example, the reference in all revision statements 2 
for the initial O-RAN models include cross-reference to “ORAN-WG5.MP.0-v01.00”.  3 
 4 
The revision statement of the YANG models also includes a description which is used to track the versioning of the 5 
YANG model. All revision statement descriptions will begin with “version ”<a>“.”<b>“.”<c>, where <a>, <b> and <c> 6 
are used to reflect the version of the YANG model, where 7 
 8 
<a> corresponds to the first digit of the O-RAN WG5 O1 interface s pecification for O -DU version where the 9 
corresponding description was first introduced, corresponding to <x> in subclause 1.1 10 
<b>  is incremented when errors in the YANG model have been corrected 11 
<c> is incremented only in working versions of the YANG mode l indicating incremental changes during the 12 
editing process 13

4 High Level Description 16 
4.1 Top level functional description, terminology, including hybrid, 17 
hierarchical 18 
4.1.1 Architecture for O-RAN WG5 functional split 19 
This O1 interface facilitates the initialization, configuration and management of the O-DU to support the functional split. 20 
Please refer to O-RAN OAM Architecture [i.5] for more details on architecture and functional split. 21 
4.1.2 O1 interface for O-DU architecture model 22 
O1 interface for O -DU is used for supporting the management features including “start up” installation, PNF software 23 
management, provisioning management, performance management, fault management and file management towards the 24 
O-DU.  25 
The O1 interface for O-DU is also used to support O-RU management. For this purpose, specific models are used to 26 
aggregate the configuration of individual O-RU functions (deployed as separate entities) and present them over the O1 27 
interface of the O-DU(s) connected to them. The management of these O-RUs may be performed according to either 28 
Hierarchical model or Hybrid model, depending on the particular deployment; see clause 12 for details regarding these 29 
two models. 30 
 31 
4.1.3 Transport Network 32 
Based on the transport topology, various modes of network connectivity are possible between O-DU and O-CU and SMO.  33 
The basic requirement for O1 interface for O-DU is to have end to end IP connectivity between the O-DU and the elements 34 
managing it. The O-DU shall support either IPv4 or IPv6 and optionally support dual stack (IPv4 and IPv6) .  35 
This version of the O1 interface for O -DU has not been defined to be able to operate in the presence of any Network 36 
Address Translation (NAT) between the O-DU and elements managing it.  37 
4.2 Interfaces 38 
The interface between the management system and the O-DU is O1. The general requirement for O1 interface for O-DU 39 
is aligned with [6], clause 4 General Requirements. 40 
Heartbeat Notification for O-DU is aligned with [6], clause 6.6.1 Heartbeat Notification. 41

5.4 NETCONF Connection Establishment 9 
5.4.1 NETCONF Authentication  10 
This version of the O1 Specification uses mutual authentication based on X.509 certificates  [3]. 11 
Mutual Public key -based client/server authentication shall be used for authenticating the server (RFC 4253  [4]) by the 12 
clients. and authenticating the client by the server. 13 
For the purposes of NETCONF user authentication, the mapping between certificates and user -names is provided by the 14 
SubjectAltName field of the X.509 certificate  [3], which means that the user name is coded in the subjectAltName. The 15 
username is determined from the subjectAltName using the rules defined in RFC 7589 [15]. 16 
Note: In RFC7589, different user-name and SubjectAltName mappings are possible. O-RAN SFG is working on extensive 17 
solution designed for O1 interface. Further alignment with gene ric O1 Interface Specification [6] will be needed once 18 
done. 19 
5.5 NETCONF Access Control 20 
This subclause provides the access control for NETCONF client. Its motivation is when multiple NETCONF clients 21 
(users) exist, access control mechanism allows to limit some operation for one client but full access for the other client.  22 
For the O1 interface, i n order to support interoperable access control management, the NETCONF Server shall follow 23 
privilege access control requirements which are specified in O -RAN Security R equirements Specification [12] clause 24 
3.2.2.1.2. 25 
For accessing O-RU YANG data models access control please refer to clause 6.5 of [2]. 26 
5.6 NETCONF Protocol Aspects 27 
5.6.1 Introduction 28 
This clause covers aspects of NETCONF protocol usage by the O-DU. For full list of supported services please refer to 29 
clause 6.1 of [6]. 30 
5.6.2 NETCONF Capability Discovery 31 
The O-DU advertises its NETCONF capabilities in the NETCONF Hello message. The Hello message provides an 32 
indication of support for standard features defined in NETCONF RFCs [i.1] as well as support for specific namespaces. 33

appropriate configuration as shown in the following example. 28

 Example: configuration of the ietf-yang-schema-mount.yang in xml format for software management. 1

7.3.2 Hybrid Model 7 
In the hybrid architecture for O-RU, this clause is not applicable as O-DU is not responsible for the SW management of 8 
O-RU. In such case, the SMO performs the software management of O-DU by [6], and the software management of O-9 
RU by O-RAN WG4 Management Plane Specification [2]. The SMO may perform the software management of O-RU 10 
by O1 Interface Specification [6] if O-RU supports [6] for its management. 11 
8 Performance Assurance Management 12 
8.1 Performance Data File Reporting 13 
Performance Data File Reporting function for O-DU is aligned with O1 Interface Specification [6] except following 14 
part. 15 
O-RU performance counters measured at O-RU: 16 
In the hierarchical architecture of O-RAN WG4 Management Plane Specification [2], O-DU as NETCONF client will 17 
control the performance measurement of O-RU as NETCONF server. The information to be collected in O-RU is also 18 
controlled by SMO via O-DU by [2]. They are defined in Annex A.14. 19 
The measured result file created by O-RU will be periodically uploaded to O-DU’s internal storage aligned with [2] and 20 
O-DU will handle it by Performance Data File Reporting function aligned with O1 interface spec [6]. As the alternative 21 
way, the measured result file created by O-RU will be forwarded to the FTP server configured by O-DU. For the latter 22 
case, Performance Assurance MnS Consumer shall provide the remote -SFTP-upload-path and its credential to O-RU 23 
that can upload the PM data file directly. 24 
8.1.1 PM File Content 25 
The Measurement Type and definitions for performance counters are described in both clause 6.3 of O1 interface 26 
specification [6] and Annex A of this specification. All measurements are optional and can be selected based on service 27 
deployment. 28 
8.1.2 PM File Naming 29 
PM file naming is specified in [6] clause 6.3.1.7.  30 
8.1.3 PM File XML Format 31 
PM file XML format is specified in [6] clause 6.3.1.8.  32 
8.2 Performance Data Streaming 33 
Performance Data Streaming for O-DU is aligned with [6] 34 
8.3 Performance Assurance Control 35 
Performance Assurance Control for “O1 interface for O-DU” is aligned with [6].  36 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        23 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 In addition to the parameters defined in Measurement Control, the following two parameters are additionally defined for 1 
O1 interface spec. 2 
- pm-count-list-drb: indicates the QoS group specific to performance assurance control for qci-index. Each entry 3 
contains qci-index [0…255] and corresponding pm-count-group [0…17]. The multiple entries with different qci-4 
index can map to same pm-count-group to combine the measurement result for them. Value 0 for pm-count-5 
group means that there is no need to collect measurement for the qci-index. 6 
- pm-count-list-srb: indicates the QoS group specific to performance assurance control for srb-index. Each entry 7 
contains srb-index [SRB1, SRB2, SRB3] and corresponding pm-count-group [0, 18…20]. Value 0 for pm-count-8 
group means that there is no need to collect measurement for the srb-index. 9 
NOTE: pm-count-group [1..20] corresponds to PmCountGroup number #0 to 19. 10

9 Fault Supervision Management 35 
9.1 General 36 
Fault Supervision Management allows a managed element to provide asynchronous Fault notification to the authorized 37 
manager of the managed element. O-DU should have a capability to send fault notifications and corresponding 38 
authorized manager should have a capability to receive and handle the fault notifications for managed element.  39 
The requirement of Fault Supervision Management is based on the Fault Supervision Management Services of O1 40 
interface specification [6] that contains 3GPP TS 28.545 [7] such as the requirement of fault notification and control. 41 
This clause describes the fault supervision management for O-DU specific aspects. 42 
General architecture of Fault Supervision Management is aligned with the Fault Supervision Management Services of 43 
O1 interface specification [6].  44 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        24 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 9.2 Definition of the Operations for Fault Events 1 
O-DU Fault Supervision Management is specified in clause 6.2.2 of O1 interface specification [6]. Fault Supervision 2 
Management subscription is specified in clause 6.1.7 of O1 interface specification [6]. 3 
9.3 Definition of Notifications as Fault Events 4 
O-DU as for Fault Supervision Data Report service producer notifies the JSON encoded asynchronous notifications to 5 
Fault Supervision MnS Consumer using REST/HTTPS. All O1 fault notification types are specified in clause 6.2.1.4 of 6 
O1 interface specification [6]. 7 
9.4 Message Format for Fault Events 8 
An O-RAN fault notification format is specified in clause 6.2.1.4 of O1 interface specification [6]. 9 
9.5 O-RU Alarms Management by O-DU in Hierarchical Model 10

O-RU alarms. O-DU receives NETCONF based alarm notification from the O-RU, converts NETCONF based alarm 12 
notification to O-RAN fault notification, updates AlarmRecords and delivers it to SMO. O-DU alarms and O-RU 13 
alarms may have the same alarm-id, they are distinguished using nfcNamingCode in the VES common event header.   14

10 File Management 5 
10.1 Introduction 6 
This clause illustrates File Management between the O-DU and the SMO/OAM. The File Management Service is 7 
applied to manage file transfer for different types of data file such as Bulk CM file, Call and UE trace file, Performance 8 
Measurement result file, etc. The following file management use cases are supported for the O-DU: 9 
• List available files 10 
• Transfer file 11 
• Download file 12 
• File ready notification 13 
The detailed description of the use cases including file management operations and procedures as well as sequence 14 
diagram can be found in the O1 Interface Specification [6], clause 6.5. 15 
This clause shall describe the handling of files that are stored in the O-DU which are generated by the O-DU itself or 16 
transferred from another server like O-RU(s). One scenario would be that files stored in the O-DU file repository are 17 
transferred from the O-RU or from some other file servers. The files handling between O-DU and O-RU are defined in 18 
the O-RAN WG4 Management Plane Specification [2].  19 
The data files that are stored in the O-DU shall follow clause 8.1 of this specification. 20 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        26 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 10.2 File Structure 1 
The file system structure for the O-DU is defined as for file management procedures defined in the rest of this clause. If 2 
the O -DU’s physical file str ucture differs from the logical file structure defined below, the O -DU shall perform  the 3 
mapping of related files into defined structure. 4 
The O-DU shall support the standardized folders for files generated by the O-DU itself and files transferred from O-RUs. 5 
The following standardized folders are defined: 6 
› O-RAN/O-DU/PM/ for performance data files 7 
› O-RAN/O-DU/CM/ for configuration files (except inventory), 8 
› O-RAN/O-DU/NL/ for notification log file 9 
› O-RAN/O-DU/CT/ for call trace files 10 
› O-RAN/O-DU/OT/ for other files 11 
› O-RAN/O-DU/O-RU<RC>/   for files from O-RU which shall follow [2] logical file structure. The RC parameter 12 
is a running count, starting with the value of "1", and shall be appended only if the filename is not unique, i.e. 13 
more than one file is generated, and all other parameters of the file name are identical. 14 
› The O-DU may additionally support vendor defined folders which are out of scope of this specification.  15 
10.3 Notification notifyFileReady 16 
The file ready notification is applied when the management data files have been prepared in  the O-DU. The O-DU will 17 
send notification using notifyFileReady VES event to subscribed SMO/OAM, in order to notify the availability of the 18 
file(s) as defined in [6]. 19 
The following input parameters are provided by the file ready notification (see also 3GPP TS 32.342 [10]): 20 
objectClass Notification header – see 3GPP TS 32.302 
[11]. It shall carry the FTIRP class name. 
objectInstance Notification header - see 3GPP TS 32.302 [11]. 
It shall carry the DN of the FTIRP. 
notificationId Notification header - see 3GPP TS 32.302 [11]. 
eventTime Notification header - see 3GPP TS 32.302 [11]. 
systemDN Notification header - see 3GPP TS 32.302 [11]. 
notificationType Notification header – see 3GPP TS 32.302 
[11]. 
fileInfoList It specifies the information of the available file. 
additionalText It carries vendor-specific semantics not defined 
in the present document. 
Table 2: Parameters list for Notification notifyFileReady 21 
 22 
When a file is available, the O-DU sends a notifyFileReady notification to the SMO using HTTP/TLS as defined in [6].  23

10.4 File Management Operation: listAvailableFiles 4 
This listAvailableFiles operation for the SMO/OAM is applied to obtain the available file list with files location and type 5 
from the O-DU by reading the AvailableFileList IOC as specified in [10]. SMO/OAM may read the O-RU available files 6 
which are already stored in the O-DU and can be represented with AvailableFileList IOC as specified in [10]. Detailed 7 
procedure can be found in clause 6.5.2 of [6]. 8 
 9 
10.5 File Management Operation: transferFile 10 
The Transfer File Service provides the capability for the SMO/OAM to transfer files from or to the O-DU. The 11 
SMO/OAM may perform this action as a result of a FileReady notification from the O -DU informing SMO/OAM that a 12 
file is now available to transfer. In any case, the file transfer is performed using a secure file transfer protocol (SFTP or 13 
FTPeS) from or to the location provided by the O-DU. The SMO/OAM triggers file transfer operation to the O-DU. 14 
Detailed procedure can be found in clause 6.5.3 of [6]. 15 
10.6 File Management Operation: downloadFile 16 
The Download File Service provides the capability for the SMO/OAM to request the O-DU to download the file(s) 17 
when the SMO/OAM has a file that needs to be downloaded. In any case, the file download is performed using a secure 18 
file transfer protocol (SFTP or FTPeS) from the location provided by the SMO/OAM. The O-DU replies to the 19 
SMO/OAM with the result of the download procedure. Detailed procedure can be found in clause 6.5.4 of [6] 20 
11 Synchronization Aspects 21 
11.1 Introduction 22 
This clause provides the Management Plane’s interactions with various aspects of the time synchronization of the O-DU. 23 
In general, the O-DU is responsible for managing its synchronization status, to select one or more synchronization input 24 
source(s) in the LLS -C1/LLS-C2/LLS-C3 deployments and act  as synchronization master in LLS -C1/LLS-C2 25 
deployments. 26 
Synchronization deployment options are defined in the [9]. 27 
O-RU synchronization is defined by WG4, refer for details to the [2]. 28 
Refer to ITU-T recommendations [i.6], [i.4], [i.2], [i.3] for details of synchronization. 29 


  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        28 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 Prerequisite is that the O-DU synchronization parameters have been provisioned to the O-DU; 1 
- Before O-DU can start to synchronize its internal clock by external timing source. 2 
- Before O-DU begins its function as master clock. 3 
Following clauses contain main parameters required for O-DU when it is receiving synchronization from external timing 4 
source. All parameters are defined in o-ran-synchronization.yang, which shall be read together with this document. 5 
11.2 Synchronization 6 
11.2.1 Synchronization status 7 
 The read-only sync-state indicates O-DU synchronization status: 8 
- LOCKED: O-DU clock timing is phase-locked to a reference timing signal. Refer also to [i.4] definition. 9 
 10 
- HOLDOVER: O-DU clock has lost its controlling reference inp ut and is using stored data, acquired while in locked 11 
operation, to control its output. Refer also to [i.4] definition. 12 
Note: HOLDOVER state is optional. 13 
 14 
- FREERUN: O-DU clock has lost its controlling reference input and the output frequency accuracy is o utside of 15 
required accuracy. Refer also to [i.4] definition. 16 
 17 
When state of O-DU synchronization changes, O-DU shall send notifyMOIAttributeValueChange notification VES event 18 
about change. 19 
 20 
O-DU shall raise appropriate alarm in case of state change to HOLDOVER or FREERUN. O-DU shall cancel alarm when 21 
state changes back to LOCKED. 22 
 23 
O-DU shall update information which timing source(s) O -DU is using to synchronize its own clock. O -DU shall update 24 
this to ptp-status, synce-status and gnss-status containers described in following clauses. 25 
 26 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        29 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 
 1 
Figure 11-1: Allowed sync state transitions 2 
Note: HOLDOVER mode is optional and depends on internal O-DU design. 3 
 4 
11.2.2 Synchronization capabilities 5 
The read-only container sync-capability tells which timing source type(s) O-DU is capable to support. 6 
11.2.3 Synchronization configuration 7 
The container sync-config contains:  8 
Configurable list sync-priority-config, which is priority order list to control O-DU to select timing source(s).  9 
Timing source types: 10 
• GNSS 11 
• PTP 12 
• SYNCE 13 
Because SyncE only provides a frequency signal, it can only be used in combination with another timing source 14 
providing phase synchronization. Specific configurable parameter synce-enabled is used to control SyncE usage. 15 
11.2.4 PTP configuration  16 
The container ptp-config contains: 17 
- needed parameters for G.8275.1 and G.8275.2 configuration. 18 


  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        30 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 • domain-number. This indicates Domain Number for PTP announce messages. 1 
• accepted-clock-classes. This is a list of PTP acceptable Clock Classes 2 
• delay-asymmetry. The parameter defines static phase error in the recovered PTP timing signal to be 3 
compensated at the device 4 
• local-priority. The parameter defines local priority. 5 
PTP profile selection of G.8275.1 or G.8275.2 6 
The container g-8275-1-config contains: 7 
- multicast-mac-address. The parameter defines the destination MAC address, used by the O -DU in the egress PTP 8 
messages. Allowed values: 9 
• FORWARDABLE (means that PTP shall use 01-1B-19-00-00-00 destination MAC address) 10 
• NONFORWARDABLE (means that PTP shall use 01-80-C2-00-00-0E destination MAC address) 11 
The container g-8275-2-config contains: 12 
- list master-ip-configuration. Defines list of ip configuration of devices acting as ptp signal source.  13 
- ip-address. The parameter defines master IP address. 14 
 15 
11.2.5 PTP status 16 
Container ptp-status contains: 17 
- reporting-period, which defines minimum time between ptp-status VES notification reports sent by O-DU. 18 
- sync-source-status, which contains status of PTP as timing source: 19 
• IN_USE - Indicates that this source is the current master clock, i.e. the clock, which the clock, controlled by 20 
the device, is synchronized to. 21 
• USABLE - Indicates that this source is an alternate master, which the clock, controlled by the device, can 22 
potentially synchronize to, i.e. clock class and priority, announced by the master clock is lower, compared to 23 
those of the clock, controlled by the device, and the clock class is accepted. 24 
• NOT_USABLE - Indicates that this source is an alternate master, which the clock, controlled by the device, 25 
has an operational connection to, but the class or priority of the master clock is higher or equal to those of 26 
the clock, controlled by the device, or the clock class is not accepted. 27 
• NOT_IN_USE - Indicates that this source is an alternate master, which the clock controlled by the device, 28 
has no operational connection to. 29 
- clock-class, which contains clock class of the clock, controlled by the O-DU 30 
- clock-identity, which is received form the PTP source 31 
- sources, which contains a list of PTP sources per local-port-number.  32 
- steps-removed, which value is received PTP Announce message stepsRemoved attribute +1.  33 
- other attributes from the PTP Announce messages. 34 
 35 
11.2.6 SyncE configuration 36 
The container synce-config contains configuration parameters for the SyncE: 37 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        31 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 - acceptance-list-of-ssm, which defines SyncE SSM values acceptable. 1 
- ssm-timeout, maximum duration in seconds for which the actual SSM value may be d ifferent than configured 2 
values.  3 
11.2.7 SyncE status 4 
Container synce-status contains: 5 
- reporting-period, which defines minimum time between synce-status VES notification reports sent by O-DU. 6 
- sync-source-status, which contains status of SyncE as timing source: 7 
• IN_USE - Indicates that this source is the current master clock, i.e. the clock, which the clock, controlled by 8 
the device, is synchronized to. 9 
• USABLE - Indicates that this source is an alternate master, which the clock, controlled by the device, can 10 
potentially synchronize to, i.e. when the clock quality of the primary SyncE signal (SSM value) is lower, 11 
when compared to the alternate master, controlled by the device, and the SSM value is accepted. 12 
• NOT_USABLE - Indicates that this source is an alternate master, which the clock, controlled by the device, 13 
has an operational connection to, but the SSM value is not accepted (i.e clock quality is not in the acceptable 14 
range). 15 
• NOT_IN_USE - Indicates that this source is an alternate SyncE clock, which the clock contr olled by the 16 
device, has no operational connection to. 17 
Note, master identity is not generally available unless ESMC is in use. 18 
- sources, which contains list of SyncE sources per local -port-number, as reference to source MAC address, from 19 
which the SyncE signal is received. 20 
11.2.8 GNSS Configuration 21 
If O-DU Yang if-feature GNSS is true and O-DU is connected to GNSS RX (e.g. having some specific non radio 22 
interface, which is an example of local PRTC), then container gnss-config contains configuration parameters for the 23 
GNSS: 24 
- enable, which defines if GNSS receiver shall be enabled or not 25 
- satellite-constellation-list, which defines list of constellations to be used to acquire synchronization : 26 
• GLONASS 27 
• GALILEO 28 
• BEIDOU 29 
• GPS 30 
11.2.9 GNSS Status 31 
If O-DU supports GNSS feature, then container gnss-status contains GNSS status parameters: 32 
- reporting-period, which defines minimum time between gnss-status VES notification reports sent by O-DU. 33 
- sync-source-status, which contains status of GNSS as timing source: 34 
• IN_USE - Indicates that this source is the current master clock, i.e. the clock, which the clock, controlled by 35 
the device, is synchronized to. 36 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        32 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 • USABLE - Indicates that this source is an alternate master, which the clock, controlled by the device, can 1 
potentially synchronize to, i.e. clock class and priority, announced by the master clock is lower, compared to 2 
those of the clock, controlled by the device, and the SSM value is accepted.  3 
• NOT_USABLE - Indicates that this source is an alternate master, which the clock, controlled by t he device, 4 
has an operational connection to, but the class or priority of the master clock is higher or equal to those of 5 
the clock, controlled by the device, or the SSM value is not accepted. 6 
• NOT_IN_USE - Indicates that this source is an alternate master,  which the clock controlled by the device, 7 
has no operational connection to. 8 
- gnss-sync-status: 9 
• SYNCHRONIZED - Indicates that GNSS functionality is synchronized. 10 
• ACQUIRING-SYNC - Indicates that GNSS functionality is acquiring sync. 11 
• ANTENNA-DISCONNECTED - Indicates that GNSS functionality has its antenna disconnected. 12 
• BOOTING - Indicates that GNSS functionality is booting. 13 
• ANTENNA-SHORT-CIRCUIT - Indicates that GNSS functionality has an antenna short circuit. 14 
 15 
11.3 Synchronization master 16 
11.3.1 Introduction 17 
O-DU acts as synchronization master for fronthaul in LLS-C1/LLS-C2 deployments. Synchronization deployment 18 
options are defined in the [9]. 19 
Prerequisite for O-DU to act as synchronization master is that O-DU´s sync-state is LOCKED. 20 
Container sync-master-capabilities contains information of O-DU capability to act as a synchronization master and 21 
needed configuration parameters. 22 
Following clauses contain main parameters required for O-DU acting as synchronization master. All parameters are 23 
defined in o-ran-synchronization.yang, which shall be read together with this document. 24 
11.3.2 Synchronization master capabilities 25 
Container sync-master-capabilities contains information of O-DU capability to act as a synchronization master: 26 
- ptp-sync-master-capabilities contains: 27 
• ptp-sync-master-supported: 28 
TRUE – O-DU can serve as PTP synchronization master. 29 
FALSE – O-DU cannot serve as PTP synchronization master. 30 
- synce-sync-master-capabilities contains: 31 
• synce-sync-master-supported: 32 
TRUE – O-DU can serve as SyncE synchronization master. 33 
FALSE – O-DU cannot serve as SyncE synchronization master. 34 
 35 
Note: [9] considers only SyncE + PTP. 36 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        33 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 11.3.3 Synchronization master configuration 1 
Container sync-master-configuration contains configuration parameters for O-DU to act as a synchronization master. 2 
- ptp-master-configuration contains configuration for PTP master: 3 
• ptp-master-enabled-local-port-numbers. This is reference to portNumber of ExternalEthernetPort to identify 4 
the port, where the PTP is provided. 5 
• domain-number. This parameter indicates Domain Number for PTP announce messages. 6 
• multicast-mac-address. This parameter indicates Ethernet MAC address to be used as destination address 7 
(forwardable, nonforwardable) 8 
• priority2. This parameter reflects value of the priority2 attribute in PTP Announce messages. 9 
- synce-master-configuration contains configuration for SyncE master: 10 
• synce-master-enabled-local-port-numbers. This is reference to portNumber of ExternalEthernetPort to 11 
identify the port, where the SyncE is provided. 12 
Note! If configuration change is applied during O-DU run time, i.e. transmission to air is ongoing, configuration change 13 
may cause service interruption. 14 
11.3.4 Master PTP status 15 
Container ptp-master-status contains  16 
- reporting-period, which defines minimum time between ptp-master-status VES notification reports sent by O-DU. 17 
- ptp-status containing PTP status and PTP message attributes. Refer to [i.2], [i.5] and o-ran-synchronization.yang. In 18 
case O-DU is synchronized using PTP, O-DU will forward PTP message attributes received from the sync-source 19 
to master port. In case O-DU is synchronized from GNSS, O-DU shall compute locally PTP message attributes to 20 
be sent on the PTP master port. 21 
 22 
11.4 O-DU and O-RU synchronization relation with cell and carrier 23 
activation / in-activation 24 
11.4.1 Cell and carrier activation 25 
O-DU sync-state and O-RU sync-state shall be LOCKED (or HOLDOVER) before O-DU is allowed to send gNB-DU 26 
Configuration Update to CU, because it contains Served NR Cells To Add/Modify/Delete IE indicating cells which O-27 
CU can activate. 28 
When O-DU receives GNB-CU CONFIGURATION UPDATE including Cells to be Activated List Item IE from CU, 29 
O-DU shall check that O-DU sync-state and O-RU sync-state are LOCKED (or HOLDOVER) before O-DU configures 30 
to O-RU the value of the parameter “active” at tx-array-carrier element / rx-array-carrier element to “ACTIVE” for the 31 
carriers serving the cell(s) requested to be activated.  32 
If O-DU sync-state is not LOCKED (and not HOLDOVER), then O-DU shall not activate any cells from Cells to be 33 
Activated List Item IE. O-DU shall report back to CU Cells failed to be activated list IE.  34 
If O-RU(s) sync-state is not LOCKED (and not HOLDOVER), then O-DU shall not activate carriers related to Cells to 35 
be Activated List Item IE, to those O-RU(s) which sync-state is not LOCKED (and not HOLDOVER). O-DU shall 36 
report back to CU Cells failed to be activated list IE for cells that O-DU did not activate carrier(s) to O-RU(s). 37 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        34 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 11.4.2 Cell and carrier in-activation 1 
When O-DU sync-state transits to FREERUN state, O-DU shall disable all carriers in all O-RUs and report to CU in 2 
gNB-DU Configuration update Cells Status IE all O-DU cells as inactive. 3 
When O-DU receives notification from O-RU that O-RU sync-state transit to FREERUN, O-DU shall disable all 4 
carriers in that O-RU and report to CU in gNB-DU Configuration update Cells Status IE all affected cells as inactive. 5 
Refer to the [9] clause 9.4.1.3 and [2] clause 15.3.3 for more details. 6 
 7 
12 Provisioning Management 8 
12.1 Introduction 9 
The requirement of Provisioning Management is described in clause 6.1 Provisioning Management Services of O1 10 
Interface Specification [6]. This clause describes the Provisioning Management for O-DU specific aspects in addition to 11 
[6].  12 
There are 2 models to be considered for configuration of O-DU: 13 
A) Hierarchical model 14 
➢ SMO configures O-DU with all instances which are necessary for O-DU and each O-RU under O-DU. 15 
These instances are based on 3GPP SA5 data model specified in 3GPP TS 28.541 [8] and O-RAN WG4 16 
Management Plane Specification [2] YANG data model. 17 
Note: This spec focuses on the model as the first step. 18 
B) Hybrid model 19 
➢ SMO configures O-DU with all instances which are necessary for O-DU and some O-RAN WG4 20 
Management Plane Specification [2] data model instances which are necessary for each O-RU under O-21 
DU to be configured by O-DU (not by SMO). In such case, SMO configures O-RUs directly using 22 
remaining [2] data model instances which don’t need to be configured via O-DU.  23 
Note: The categorize of [2] data model instances (either via O-DU or not) is for further study, and this 24 
spec will reflect the agreement in future release. 25 
 26 
12.2 Configuration for Hierarchical Model 27 
12.2.1 Configuration Step 28 
 29 
Configuration steps for hierarchical model are following: 30 
 31 
Step1: SMO configures the instances to O-DU 32 
Regarding the data model configured from SMO, there are 4 types: 33 
1. 3GPP SA5 data model 34 
Following modules are necessary since these are related to O-DU. See TS 28.541 [8] 35 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        35 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 - _3gpp-common-managed-element.yang 1 
- _3gpp-nr-nrm-gnbdufunction.yang 2 
- _3gpp-nr-nrm-nrcelldu.yang 3 
- _3gpp-nr-nrm-ep.yang 4 
- _3gpp-nr-nrm-nrsectorcarrier.yang 5 
- _3gpp-nr-nrm-bwp.yang 6 
- _3gpp-nr-nrm-beam.yang 7 
- _3gpp-nr-nrm-commonbeamformingfunction.yang 8 
2. O-RAN WG5 modified model based on 3GPP SA5 9 
These are added prefix “o-ran-“ to the module name of 3GPP SA5.  10 
Note: Additional instances should be expected to be proposed to 3GPP for having alignment between 3GPP 11 
and O-RAN WG5. Study on the model will be included in the next version of this specification. 12 
3. O-RAN WG4 data model 13 
O-RAN WG4 data model instances which cannot be mapped from SA5 data model and cannot be created by 14 
O-DU’s internal logic, needs to be set from SMO to O-DU by aggregation model based on O-RAN WG4 15 
data model. Which parameters needs to be configured from SMO is described in Annex D 16 
4. O-RAN WG5 original data model 17 
O-RAN WG5 introduces original data model in order to configure instances which are related to fronthaul 18 
operation at O-DU side (such as O-DU transmission/reception window). 3GPP does not assume non 19 
integrated O-DU, so O-RAN WG5 introduces original model for supporting fronthaul operations.  20 
Note: These modules are not expected to be proposed to 3GPP since these are for fronthaul management 21 
operation and 3GPP does not assume fronthaul management. This version includes o-ran-wg5-delay-22 
management.yang. Whether other modules are necessary or not will be studied in the next version of this 23 
specification. 24 
 25 
 26 
Step2: O-DU configures to O-RU 27 
O-DU configures to O-RU by several ways: 28 
1. Mapping 3GPP SA5 parameters to WG4 parameters. 29 
2. Creating WG4 parameters by internal logic 30 
3. Configuring based on aggregation model 31 
 32 
These categories are specified in Annex D.  33

12.5 Notification aspect in hierarchical model 3 
12.5.1 Introduction 4 
There are 2 topics to be specified in this specification on notification aspect : 5 
- Subscribing for the O-RU notification from the SMO 6 
➢ Subscription for the O-RU notification specified in WG4 M-Plane specification [2] shall be done 7 
by the O-DU and corresponding parameters values shall be stored in the aggregated model of the 8 
O-RU. The SMO shall subscribe for parameters of interest changes from the O -RU aggregated 9 
model. 10 
- Forwarding the notification from O-RU via O-DU 11 
➢ Some of the O-RU notification specified in WG4 M-Plane specification [2] should be forwarded to 12 
the SMO via the O-DU. In such case the SMO will receive notifications from the O-DU, after 13 
subscribing to the parameters of interest from the O-RU aggregated model.  14 
Note: Some of the notifications are not necessary to be forwarded to the SMO via the O -DU since 15 
it is enough to be noticed by the O-DU. In such case it is not needed for the SMO to make 16 
subscription to those parameters in the O-RU aggregated model. 17 
 18 
Note: In Hybrid model, no additional description is necessary in this spec since O -RU can send notification to SMO 19 
directly (no need to send notification via O-DU). 20 
 21 
12.5.2 Subscribing for O-RU notification from SMO 22 
The O-DU is responsible for representing parameters of the O-RU using aggregated YANG model. The SMO is 23 
responsible of subscribing to the parameters of interest from aggregated model using subscription mechanism described 24 
in O1 Interface specification [6] clause 6.1.7 Subscription Control.  25 
12.5.3 Forwarding the notification from O-RU via O-DU 26 
Once the SMO is subscribed to the parameters of interest as described in clause 12.5.2 of this specification, the SMO 27 
will receive notification about each value change of parameter(s) in the O -DU. 28

13 Fronthaul Delay Management Support 1 
O-RAN WG4 [2] specifies delay management between O-DU and O-RU, where transmission of data over fronthaul is 2 
governed by O-DU transmission/reception window and O-RU transmission/reception window. O-RU 3 
transmission/reception window is decided by O-RU itself, and the relevant procedures and data models are specified in 4 
WG4 spec [2]. This clause addresses how O-DU transmission/reception window can be determined and the relevant 5 
procedures and data models. 6 
  7 
O-DU may support the following alternatives: 8 
A) Not Configured by O1 9 
➢ O-DU determines O-DU transmission/reception window. How O-DU determines the window is up to O-10 
DU, it may be hardcoded value at O-DU, or calculated from O-RU transmission/reception window and 11 
FH delay based on O-RAN WG4 Management Plane Specification [2]. 12 
Note: WG4 IOT profile describes O-DU transmission/reception window values. O-DU 13 
transmission/reception window can be hardcoded based on these values.   14 
➢ There is no impact to this specification, since O-DU transmission/reception window is determined at O-15 
DU. 16 
B) Configured by O1 17 
➢ SMO configures the O-DU transmission/reception window by O1. The SMO configured parameters 18 
should be taken by the O-DU as the maximum or minimum allowed values for the respective 19 
transmission/reception window parameters. Having the SMO configure maximum or minimum allowed 20 
values instead of the exact value, provides necessary flexibility for the O-DU implementation. SMO may 21 
take into account O-RU reported window and FH delay to determine O-DU transmission/reception 22 
window. 23 
➢ There is impact to this specification, where the details are described below. 24 
 25 
Note: This version focuses on hierarchical model. Next version will include hybrid model since this scheme can be 26 
extended to hybrid model. 27 
 28 
Pre-condition 29 
- Connection is established between SMO - O-DU / O-DU - O-RU 30 
Post -condition 31 
- Delay management between O-DU and O-RU is operational 32 
 33 
Steps of Fronthaul delay management support are as follows: 34 
1. SMO sends <rpc><get><window-determine-capability> to O-DU for getting the capability of O-DU 35 
2. O-DU replies the rpc with O-DU’s capability. There are 3 capabilities: 36 
Not-Configured: O-DU transmission/reception window can be determined by O-DU 37 
Configured: O-DU transmission/reception window can be determined by configured value from SMO 38 
Both: O-DU has both capabilities, Not-Configured and Configured 39 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        41 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 3. SMO decides the method how O-DU transmission/reception window is determined from capability supported 1 
by O-DU 2 
4. SMO sends <rpc><edit-config><window-determine-method> based on the decision of step3. 3 
5. In parallel with step1,2,3, O-DU gets O-RU transmission/reception window based on O-RAN WG4 4 
specification [2] 5 
6. If SMO directs Not-Configured as window-determine-method to O-DU at step4, O-DU 6 
transmission/reception window is determined by O-DU. How O-DU determines the window is up to O-DU, it 7 
may be hardcoded value at O-DU, or calculated from O-RU transmission/reception window and FH delay 8 
based on O-RAN WG4 CUS spec [9]. If SMO has pre-configured FH delay, SMO sends it in rpc window-9 
determine-method for O-DU to calculate O-DU transmission/reception window. 10 
7. If SMO directs Configured as window-determine-method to O-DU at step4,  11 
1. SMO sends <rpc><get><o-ru-window> and/or <measured-transport-delay> to O-DU as necessary 12 
(SMO may have such information apriori and may not need to get them from O -DU). 13 
2. SMO determines O-DU transmission/reception window taking into account the following WG4 14 
instances: 15 
• FH delay (pre-defined or measured): 16 
- t12-min, t12-max, 17 
- t34-min, t-34max 18 
• O-RU transmission/reception window: 19 
- t2a-min-up, t2a-max-up 20 
- t2a-min-cp-dl, t2a-max-cp-dl 21 
- tcp-adv-dl 22 
- ta3-min, ta3-max 23 
- t2a-min-cp-ul, t2a-max-cp-ul  24 
SMO determines the following parameters for O-DU transmission/reception window: 25 
•  maximum-t1a-max-up: 26 
➢ the maximum allowed value of T1a_max_up 27 
•  minimum-t1a-min-up:  28 
➢ the minimum allowed value of T1a_min_up 29 
•  maximum-t1a-max-cp-dl:  30 
➢ the maximum allowed value of T1a_max_cp_dl 31 
•  minimum-t1a-min-cp-dl: 32 
➢ the minimum allowed value of T1a_min_cp_dl 33 
•  maximum-t1a-max-cp-ul:  34 
➢ the maximum allowed value of T1a_max_cp_ul 35 
•  minimum-t1a-min-cp-ul:  36 
➢ the minimum allowed value of T1a_min_cp_ul 37 
• maximum-ta4-max:  38 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        42 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 ➢ the minimum allowed value of Ta4_max 1 
• minimum-ta4-min:  2 
➢ the maximum allowed value of Ta4_min 3 
Note: The above maximum or minimum allowed values for the respective O-DU transmission/reception 4 
window parameters that the SMO determines should satisfy the relations specified in 4.4.3 U-Plane/ C-5 
Plane Timing in O-RAN WG4 CUS-Plane Specification [9].  6 
3. SMO sends <rpc><edit-config><o-du-window> with determined maximum or minimum allowed 7 
values for the respective O-DU transmission/reception window parameters at the previous step. 8 
4. O-DU sets O-DU transmission/reception window based on o-du-window from SMO.  9 
8. If O-RU has the capability to set O-RU transmission/reception window adaptively as specified at 7.8 O-RU 10 
Adaptive Delay Capability in O-RAN WG4 M-Plane spec, O-DU sends O-DU transmission/reception window 11 
and FH delay to O-RU. O-RU may set O-RU transmission/reception window adaptively based on O-DU 12 
transmission/reception window and FH delay. 13 
9. Delay management between O-DU and O-RU is operational 14 
 15 
 16 
 17

        43

15 Shared O-RU 22 
15.1 Introduction 23 
A Shared O-RU deployment allows one or more operators to connect their O-DUs to an O-RU and share its resources. 24 
An O-DU should simultaneously support connections to non-Shared O-RUs, Multi O-DU O-RUs and/or Multi-Operator 25 
O-RUs, dependent on which Shared O-RU features the O-DU supports. 26 
Refer to [2] for more details of Shared O-RU. 27 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        45 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 15.2 Single Operator Shared O-RU  1 
15.2.1 O-DU(s) roles 2 
In Single Operator Shared O-RU deployment, O-DUs do not have specific access privilege roles as in Multi-Operator 3 
Shared O-RU. O-DUs use the same access control groups as in non-Shared O-RU. 4 
In hierarchical deployment, O-DUs all use the same access control group “sudo” toward the Multi O-DU O-RU. One O-5 
DU acts as primary O-DU responsible for configuring general OAM related configuration, supervision per O -DU, 6 
NETCONF call home and managing general OAM functions. 7 
Refer to clause 12 and [2] clause 6.5 for further details. 8 
 9 
15.2.2 Configuring O-RU  10 
15.2.2.1 Configuring O-RU general OAM related configuration 11 
In hierarchical deployment, it is recommended that SMO configures general OAM related configuration for each Multi 12 
O-DU O-RU using O1 toward only one sharing O-DU (primary). That O-DU then consequently uses the configuration 13 
data to configure the Multi O-DU O-RU over its fronthaul interface. If SMO configures the same Multi O-DU O-RU 14 
through more than one sharing O-DU, it is recommended that SMO validates outside of the O-DUs that the 15 
configuration is aligned in all the sharing O-DUs to avoid configuration discrepancy. How validation is done is out of 16 
the scope of the present document. 17 
NOTE: O-RU does not check which O-DU(s) is configuring it, nor does it validate if e.g., same parameter is 18 
configured to different allowed values by O-DUs. 19 
In hybrid deployment, it is recommended that SMO directly configures all general OAM related configuration for each 20 
Multi O-DU O-RU over its Fronthaul M-plane interface.  21 
Refer to clause 12 for further details. 22 
 23 
15.2.2.2 Managing O-RU general OAM related functions 24 
In hierarchical deployment, it is recommended that SMO manages Multi O-DU O-RU general OAM functions using O1 25 
toward only one sharing O-DU (primary), for example: software management, file Management, synchronization 26 
aspects, antenna line devices, operational aspects of external IO, O-RU connectors, beamforming configuration update, 27 
user account provisioning. If SMO manages general OAM functions for the same Multi O-DU O-RU through more than 28 
one sharing O-DU, it is recommended that SMO co-ordinates the O-DUs that the management is aligned in all of the 29 
sharing O-DUs to avoid discrepancy. How validation is done is out of the scope of the present document.  30 
In hybrid deployment, it is recommended that SMO directly manages all Multi O-DU O-RU general OAM functions for 31 
each Multi O-DU O-RU over its Fronthaul M-plane interface. 32 
O-DUs may manage other O-RU functions independently e.g., NETCONF connection establishment, performance 33 
management, fault management, static configuration for PRACH and SRS.  34 
Refer to clause 12 and [2] clauses 8, 12, 13, 14.4, 14.5, 14.6, 15.4 for further details. 35 
 36 
15.2.2.3 Configuring carrier configuration 37 
SMO shall configure only the cells that the O-DU serves and their corresponding carriers over O1 towards that O-DU. 38 
The O-DU shall then consequently configure the corresponding tx/rx-array-carriers on the Multi O-DU O-RUs over 39 
their fronthaul interfaces. 40 
 41 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        46 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 15.2.2.4 Carrier state management 1 
An O-DU shall only activate or deactivate the tx/rx-array-carriers on the Shared O-RU that belongs to the cells that the 2 
O-DU serves. 3 
When an O-DU receive a notification from a Shared O-RU indicating tx/rx-array-carrier state change, the O-DU shall 4 
treat the notification in the same way as for a non-shared O-RU, i.e., O-DU shall ignore the notifications that do not 5 
relate to the O-DU cell´s NRSectorCarriers. 6 
 7 
15.2.3 Supervision Monitoring per O-DU 8 
In hierarchical deployment, SMO may configure SecondaryODuInfo including attribute supervisionPerODu over O1 on 9 
the primary O-DU. The primary O-DU shall then consequently configure Shared Resource Operator O-DU supervision 10 
on each Shared O-RU. 11 
In hybrid deployment, SMO instead may configure Shared Resource Operator O-DU supervision directly on each 12 
Shared O-RU over its Fronthaul M-plane interface.  13 
Refer to [2] clause 6.7, 19.3.4 for further details. 14 
 15 
15.2.4 NETCONF call home 16 
In hierarchical deployment, SMO may configure the SecondaryODuInfo including attribute callHomeClientInfo over 17 
O1 only on the primary O-DU. If callHomeClientInfo has been configured, the primary O-DU shall then consequently 18 
configure call home addresses on each Shared O-RU. 19 
In hybrid deployment, SMO instead may configure call home addresses directly on each Shared O-RU over its 20 
Fronthaul M-plane interface.  21 
 22 
15.3 Multi Operator Shared O-RU  23 
15.3.1 O-DU(s) roles 24 
O-DU possible roles towards a Multi Operator Shared O-RU are defined in [2]. O-DU role towards all connected Multi 25 
Operator Shared O-RUs is configured over O1 by setting oDuRoleOfSharedORu to one of the values: 26 
“HOST_AND_SRO”, “HOST” or “SRO”.  27 
When O-DU role is set to “HOST_AND_SRO”, the O-DU simultaneously perform the Shared O-RU Host role and the 28 
Shared Resource Operator roles towards all connected Multi Operator Shared O -RUs. 29 
When O-DU role is set to “HOST”, the O-DU only performs the Shared O-RU Host role, equaling Neutral Host. That 30 
O-DU configures and manages all connected Multi Operator Shared O-RUs but does not have carriers in those O-RUs. 31 
For each Multi Operator Shared O-RU, at most only one connected O-DU should perform the Shared O-RU Host role. 32 
If no connected O-DU performs the Shared O-RU Host role, it is assumed that an SMO performs that role, acting as 33 
Neutral Host. However, the scenario in which the Neutral Host is provided by SMO is not considered in this version of 34 
the document. 35 
In a hierarchical deployment containing Multi Operator Shared O-RUs, the O-DU performing the Shared O-RU Host 36 
role uses the access control group “sudo” toward all connected Multi Operator Shared O -RUs. The O-DUs performing 37 
only the Shared Resource Operator role (i.e., not together with the Shared O -RU Host role) use the access control group 38 
“carrier” towards all connected Multi Operator Shared O-RUs. 39 
In a hybrid deployment containing Multi Operator Shared O-RUs, if an O-DU performs the Shared O-RU Host role, it 40 
uses the access control group “hybrid-odu” toward the Multi O-DU O-RU. The O-DUs performing only the Shared 41 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        47 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 Resource Operator role (i.e., not together with the Shared O-RU Host role) use the access control group “carrier” 1 
towards all connected Multi Operator Shared O-RUs.  2 
Following sub-clauses define what shall be configured over O1 to O-DU to realize O-DU functions defined in [2]. 3 
 4 
15.3.2 Configuring O-RU general OAM related configuration 5 
In hierarchical deployment, it is recommended that SMO configures O-RU general OAM related configuration over O1 6 
toward only the single Shared O-RU Host O-DU. The Shared O-RU Host O-DU shall then consequently configure 7 
general OAM related configuration on the Multi Operator O-RUs over their fronthaul interfaces. 8 
In hybrid deployment, it is recommended that SMO directly configures general OAM related configuration  for each 9 
Multi O-DU O-RU over its Fronthaul M-plane interface. 10 
 11 
15.3.3 Managing O-RU general OAM related functions 12 
In hierarchical deployment, it is recommended that SMO manages O-RU general OAM related functions over O1 13 
toward only the single shared O-RU Host O-DU. The Shared O-RU Host O-DU shall then consequently manage 14 
general OAM related functions on the Multi Operator O-RUs over their fronthaul interfaces. 15 
In hybrid deployment, it is recommended that SMO directly manages Multi O-DU O-RU general OAM functions for 16 
each Multi O-DU O-RU over its Fronthaul M-plane interface. 17 
 18 
15.3.4 NETCONF server user account provisioning for shared resource 19 
operators 20 
In hierarchical deployment, SMO shall configure the SecondaryODuInfo over O1 only on the Shared O -RU Host O-21 
DU. The Shared O-RU Host O-DU shall then consequently configure Shared Resource Operator user accounts with 22 
“carrier” access privilege and sro-id=sharedResourceOperatorId on the connected Multi Operator O-RUs over their 23 
fronthaul interfaces. 24 
NOTE: Value of each sharedResourceOperatorId shall be unique and associated with a particular Shared Resource 25 
Operator only. 26 
In hybrid deployment, SMO instead configures Shared Resource Operator user accounts with “carrier” access privilege 27 
and sro-id=sharedResourceOperatorId directly on each Multi Operator O-RU over its Fronthaul M-plane interface. 28 
Refer to [2] clause 19.3.1 for further details. 29 
 30 
15.3.5 NETCONF call home 31 
In hierarchical deployment, SMO may configure the SecondaryODuInfo including attribute callHomeClientInfo over 32 
O1 only on the Shared O-RU Host O-DU. If callHomeClientInfo has been configured, the Shared O-RU Host O-DU 33 
shall then consequently configure call home addresses on each Shared O -RU. 34 
In hybrid deployment, SMO instead may configure call home addresses directly on each Shared O-RU using its 35 
Fronthaul M-plane interface.  36 
Refer to [2] clause 19.3.2 for further details. 37

 15.3.6 Enhanced sro-id based NETCONF access control 1 
SMO shall configure the attribute sharedResourceOperatorId over O1 with a unique value on each Shared Resource 2 
Operator O-DU. The Shared Resource Operator O-DU shall then consequently use the value of 3 
sharedResourceOperatorId for the user account of the NETCONF client with sro-id configured on the Multi Operator 4 
Shared O-RUs. 5 
Refer to [2] clause 19.3.3 for further details. 6 
 7 
15.3.7 Supervision Monitoring per O-DU 8 
In hierarchical deployment, SMO may configure SecondaryODuInfo including attribute supervisionPerODu over O1 on 9 
the Shared O-RU Host. The Shared O-RU Host shall then consequently configure Shared Resource Operator O-DU 10 
supervision on each Shared O-RU. 11 
In hybrid deployment, SMO instead may configure Shared Resource Operator O-DU supervision directly on each 12 
Shared O-RU using its Fronthaul M-plane interface.  13 
Refer to [2] clause 6.7, 19.3.4 for further details. 14 
 15 
15.3.8 Processing element configuration 16 
Shared O-RU Host O-DU shall use the value of each Shared Resource Operator O-DUs sharedResourceOperatorId 17 
attribute to configure a particular O-RU´s ru-element list entry as being uniquely associated with a particular Shared 18 
Resource Operator. Shared O-RU Host O-DU gets sharedResourceOperatorId as defined in 13.3.6. 19 
Refer to [2] clause 19.4.2. 20 
 21 
15.3.9 Carrier Partitioning and Configuration in Shared O-RU 22 
Only Shared O-RU Host O-DU has access privileges over Fronthaul M-plane to create tx/rx-array-carrier configuration 23 
in the Shared O-RU. 24 
NOTE: How Shared Resource Operators agree configuration partitioning is outside the scope of the present 25 
document. It is assumed that operators mutually agree partitioning. 26 
NOTE: How Shared Resource Operators configurations are validated is outside the scope of the present document. 27 
It is assumed that operators mutually validate as part of configuration partitioning.  28 
NOTE: How Shared Resource Operators agree eAxC-IDs partitioning is out of the scope of the present document. It 29 
is assumed that operators mutually agree partitioning. 30 
Refer to clause 12.1 and [2] clause 19.6.1, 19.11. 31 
 32 
15.3.10 Notification of configuration updates 33 
A Shared Resource Operator O-DU may configure subscriptions to receive notifications of modifications to a connected 34 
shared O-RU’s datastore, according to the defined NETCONF access control privileges for the NETCONF client of that 35 
Shared Resource Operator. 36 
Refer to clause 12 and [2] clause 19.6.2 for further details. 37

Co-ordination of Shared O-RU reset is outside the scope of the current specification.  2

administrative state to locked. 10 
NOTE: It is assumed that SMO(s) disable cell(s) in a controlled manner before Shared O -RU state is changed to 11 
locked. 12

Co-ordination of Shared O-RU antenna calibration timing is outside the scope of the current specification.  16 
NOTE: It is assumed that operators mutually agree timing for Shared O -RU antenna calibrations. 17 
Refer to [2] clause 19.10.3 for further details. 18 
 19 
15.3.14 Shared O-RU with antenna line devices 20 
The Shared O-RU Host O-DU is responsible for configuring and controlling antenna line devices. 21 
NOTE: It is assumed that operators mutually share antenna line devices configuration and co -ordinate antenna line 22 
operations e.g., remote electrical tilt. 23 
Refer to [2] clause 14.4, 19.11.6. 24 
 25 
15.3.15 Shared O-RU operation in combination with shared cell 26 
The Shared O-RU Host O-DU is responsible for configuring shared cell copy and combine parameters on behalf of each 27 
Shared Resource Operator O-DU. 28 
NOTE: How Shared Resource Operators agree Shared Cell configuration of copy and combine is outside the scope 29 
of the present document. It is assumed that operators mutually agree partitioning.  30 
Refer to [2] clause 17, 19.14 for further details. 31

 15.4 Content of Fronthaul M-plane ODU ID 1 
O-DU uses the value of the attribute oDuIdForSharedORu as the Fronthaul M-plane odu-id, which is a free text string 2 
and can be set to e.g.., concatenated gNBId and gNBDUId.  3 
 4 
15.5 Content of Fronthaul M-plane SRO ID 5 
O-DU uses the value of the attribute sharedResourceOperatorId as the Fronthaul M-plane sro-id, which is a free text 6 
string and can be set to e.g.., PLMN ID. 7

17 O-DU behavior for 3GPP conformance testing 2 
17.1 Introduction 3 
This clause describes O-DU behavior to evaluate O-RU performance based on the 3GPP standardized conformance 4 
tests.  5 
To guarantee the minimum performance of gNB, O-RAN WG5 follows tests definition from [16], [17], and [18].  6 
Any points not mentioned in this clause are expected to be in accordance with the corresponding test specifications in 7 
[16], [17], and [18].  8 
Note: The present version of this specification considers only PNF-deployed O-DU. 9 
17.2 O-DU behavior for O-RU uplink evaluation 10 
O-DU behavior for uplink tests specified in clauses 7 and 8 in [18] is as follows: 11 
Step 1: O-DU receives a request, by O1, to conduct a test with the configuration parameters defined in Table 12 of 12 
Annex E. 13 
Step 2: In the test mode, when receiving signals from O-RU for a certain measurement period, O-DU counts 14 
measurements shown in Table 12 of Annex E.  15 
Step 3: O-DU reports the measurements results by O1 as PM counters specified in Annex A. After finishing reporting, 16 
O-DU exits the test mode. 17 
Note: A test of “Receiver spurious emissions” defined in clause 7.6 in [18] is not applicable to the above steps as it is 18 
not measured at the O-DU. 19 
17.3 O-DU behavior for O-RU downlink evaluation 20 
O-DU behavior for downlink tests specified in clause 6 in [18] is as follows: 21 
Step 1: O-DU receives a request, by O1, to conduct a test with the configuration parameters defined in Table 13 of 22 
Annex E. 23 
Step 2: In the test mode, O-DU generates test data and sends it to O-RU over CU-Plane of the Open Fronthaul interface. 24 
After sending test data, the O-DU exits the test mode. 25 
Note: O-DU doesn’t measure parameters in downlink tests because test results will be collected by the measurement 26 
equipment such as a spectrum analyzer. 27 
 28 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        58 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 
Annex A (informative): 1 
Counter definition  2 
A.1 NR F1 Interface performance counters 3 
A.1.1 UL PDCP PDUs transmitted via F1-U UL GTP-U tunnel 4 
A.1.1.1 Performance Counter Table 5 
Measurement Name OR.F1.UlPdcpPduTxF1UUl 
Description This counter provides the number of the UL PDCP PDUs transmitted via 
F1-U UL GTP-U tunnel.  
It is optional counter for O-DU. 
Collection Method CC (Cumulative Counter) 
Condition Measurement subcounter is incremented by 1 whenever the UL PDCP 
PDU is transmitted via F1 U UL GTP-u tunnel when the QCI or the 5QI 
of the UL PDCP PDU is group of subcounter.Pmgroup. 
Measurement Result Integer number (U32) 
Measurement Type OR.F1.UlPdcpPduTxF1UUl.Pmgroup where 
PmGroup is PmCountGroup number: 
0: #0 
1: #1 
… 
19: #19 
Measurement Object Class gNBDUFunction

 A.4 NR UL HARQ performance counters 1 
A.4.1 Distribution of PUSCH per MCS (initial transmission) 2 
A.4.1.1 Performance Counter Table 3 
Measurement Name OR.ULHARQ.DistPuschMcsInitial 
Description This counter provides the distributions of PUSCH at the initial 
transmission per MCS. 
It is optional counter for O-DU. 
Collection Method CC (Cumulative Counter) 
Condition Measurement subcounter is incremented by 1 whenever PUSCH is 
received for initial transmission when the MCS table of the PUSCH is 
group of subcounter.MCSTable and when the MCS index of the PUSCH 
is group of subcounter.MCSInitial. 
Measurement Result Integer number (U32) 
Measurement Type OR.ULHARQ.DistPuschMcsInitial.MCSInitial.MCSTable where 
MCSInitial is the MCS index for initial transmission: 
0: IMCS = 0 
1: IMCS = 1 
… 
28: IMCS = 28 
MCSTable is the MCS table: 
0: MCS index table 1 for PDSCH/PUSCH without transform 
precoding 
1: MCS index table 2 for PDSCH/PUSCH without transform 
precoding 
2: MCS index table 3 for PDSCH/PUSCH without transform 
precoding 
3: MCS index table for PUSCH with transform precoding and 64QAM 
(q=1) 
4: MCS index table for PUSCH with transform precoding and 64QAM 
(q=2) 
5: MCS index table 2 for PUSCH with transform precoding and 
64QAM(q=1) 
6: MCS index table 2 for PUSCH with transform precoding and 
64QAM (q=2) 
Measurement Object Class NRCellDU 
Switching Technology Packet Switched 
Generation 5GS 
Purpose Network Operator’s Traffic Engineering Community

A.6.5 PUSCH received power 2 
A.6.5.1 Performance Counter Table 3 
Measurement Name OR.ULSQL.PuschRxPower 
Description This counter measures the following x and provides round(x, 2)･102. x is 
the statistics of received power of FL DMRS of PUSCH. This counter 
obtains the power for every slot or mini slot in which PUSCH reception 
is expected. The power is normalized by PRB and antenna port. If Rx 
beam is created by some antenna ports, this counter is calculated with the 
power of only the antenna ports used to create Rx beam. 
It is recommended to support for O-DU. 
Collection Method SI (Status Inspection) 
Condition Measurement subcounter of subcounter.statistic(avg.) is calculated by 
round(x/y, 2) * 102, where: 
x is incremented by the volume of power of front loaded DMRS of 
PUSCH whenever PUSCH reception is expected when SSB used 
for PUSCH is group of subcounter.SSB. The power is normalized 
by PRB and antenna port. If Rx beam is created by some antenna 
ports, this counter is calculated with the power of only the antenna 
ports used to create Rx beam. 
y is incremented by 1 whenever PUSCH reception is expected when 
SSB used for PUSCH is group of subcounter.SSB.  
Measurement subcounter of subcounter.statistic(max/min) is 
maximum/minimum number of round(z, 2) * 102 . It is assigned 
whenever z is updated by the volume round(z, 2) * 102, if round(z, 2) * 
102 is bigger/smaller than previously counted volume, where: 
z is the volume of power of front loaded DMRS of PUSCH whenever 
PUSCH reception is expected when SSB used for PUSCH is group of 
subcounter.SSB. The power is normalized by PRB and antenna port. If 
Rx beam is created by some antenna ports, this counter is calculated 
with the power of only the antenna ports used to create Rx beam. 
Measurement Result dBm/102 (S16) 
Measurement Type OR.ULSQL.PuschRxPower.SSB.statistic where SSB is the SSB index: 
0: #0 
1: #1 
… 
63: #63 
statistic is 
0: average 
1: maximum 
2: minimum 
Measurement Object Class NRCellDU 
Switching Technology Packet Switched 
Generation 5GS 
Purpose Network Operator’s Traffic Engineering Community

A.6.10 PRACH preamble correlation value 2 
A.6.10.1 Performance Counter Table 3 
Measurement Name OR.ULSQL.PrachPreambleCorrelationValue 
Description This counter measures the following x and provides round(x, 2) ･102. x 
is the statistics of the correlation value among preambles of the PRB 
where PRACH preabmble is detected. This counter normalized by PRB.  
It is recommended to support for O-DU. 
Collection Method SI (Status Inspection) 
Condition Measurement subcounter of subcounter.statistic(avg.) is calculated by 
round(x/y, 2) * 102, where: 
x is incremented by the correlation volume among preambles of 
the PRB whenever PRACH preamble is detected when SSB used 
for PRACH is group of subcounter.SSB. 
y is incremented by 1 whenever PRACH preamble is detected when 
SSB used for PRACH is group of subcounter.SSB. 
Measurement subcounter of subcounter.statistic(max/min) is 
maximum/minimum number of round(z, 2) * 102. It is assigned 
whenever z is updated by the volume round(z, 2) * 102, if round(z, 2) *

A.7.11 PDCCH transmission power 2 
A.7.11.1 Performance Counter Table 3 
Measurement Name OR.DLSQL.PdcchTxPower 
Description This counter measures the following x and provides round(x, 2) ･102. x 
is the statistics of transmission power determined by outer-loop TPC of 
UE specific PDCCH. If PDCCH is transmitted within some OFDM 
symbols with same SSB in one slot, this counter counts 1 sample and 
calculates power as linear average within OFDM symbols. If PDCCH is 
transmitted with different SSB each OFDM symbols in the one slot, this 
counter counts the PDCCH for each SSB, and doesn't calculate power as 
average within OFDM symbols. 
It is optional counter for O-DU. 
Collection Method SI (Status Inspection) 
Condition Measurement subcounter of subcounter.statistic(avg.) is calculated by 
round(x/y, 2) * 102, where: 
x is incremented by the volume of transmission power of PDCCH 
whenever PDCCH is transmitted when SSB used for PDCCH is 
group of subcounter.SSB and when the DCI format of transmitted 
DCI is group of subcounter.DCI. If PDCCH is transmitted within 
plural OFDM symbols with same SSB in one slot, the volume is linear 
average within the OFDM symbols. If PDCCH is transmitted with 
different SSB in each OFDM symbols in the one slot, x is incremented 
for each one. 
y is incremented by 1 whenever PDCCH is transmitted when SSB 
used for PDCCH is group of subcounter.SSB and when the DCI 
format of transmitted DCI is group of subcounter.DCI. If PDCCH is 
transmitted within plural OFDM symbols with same SSB in one slot, y 
is only incremented once per slot. If PDCCH is transmitted with 
different SSB in each OFDM symbols in the one slot, y is incremented 
once per OFDM symbol. 
Measurement subcounter of subcounter.statistic(max/min) is 
maximum/minimum number of round(z, 2) * 102. It is assigned 
whenever z is updated by the volume round(z, 2) * 102, if round(z, 2) * 
102 is bigger/smaller than previously counted volume, where: 
z is the volume of transmission power of PDCCH whenever 
PDCCH is transmitted when SSB used for PDCCH is group of 

  
Copyright © 2024 O-RAN ALLIANCE e.V. Your use is subject to copyright statement on the cover page of this specification 
        102 
O-RAN.WG5.O-DU-O1.0-R003-v09.00 
 
 subcounter.SSB and when the DCI format of transmitted DCI is 
group of subcounter.DCI. If PDCCH is transmitted within plural 
OFDM symbols with same SSB in one slot, the volume is linear 
average within OFDM symbols. If PDCCH is transmitted with 
different SSB in each OFDM symbols in the one slot, z is once per 
OFDM symbol. 
Measurement Result dBm/102 (S16) 
Measurement Type OR.DLSQL.PdcchTxPower.SSB.DCI.statistic where SSB is the SSB 
index: 
0: #0 
1: #1 
… 
63: #63 
DCI is the DCI format: 
0: 0_0 
1: 0_1 
2: 1_0 
3: 1_1 
statistic is 
0: average 
1: maximum 
2: minimum 
Measurement Object Class NRCellDU 
Switching Technology Packet Switched 
Generation 5GS 
Purpose Network Operator’s Traffic Engineering Community

 A.8.2 Best and Second Best Beam distribution 1 
A.8.2.1 Performance Counter Table 2 
Measurement Name OR.BF.BestSecondBestBeamDist 
Description This counter provides the distribution of Best and Second best beams. 
This counter is only updated when number of SSB is 8 or less. 
This is optional counter for O-DU. 
Collection Method CC (Cumulative Counter) 
Condition  Measurement subcounter is incremented by the number of the UEs per 
the best and second best SSB index of the UE: best beam #0 and second 
beam #0, best beam #1 and second beam #0, …, best beam#7 and second 
beam#7 as subcounter.binX. 
The value for a given bin shall be incremented when either best or 
second best beam is changed for any reason. 
Measurement Result Integer number (U16) 
Measurement Type OR.BF.BestSecondBestBeamDist.binX where 
Bin1 is best beam #0 and second beam #0. 
Bin2 is best beam #1 and second beam #0. 
: 
BinX is best beam #a and second beam #b. :X = a+8b+1 
: 
Bin64 is best beam#7 and second beam#7.

... 
bin10: 654885 ≤ NTA 
CellSize = middle: 
bin1: 0 ≤ NTA < 29106 
bin2: 29106 ≤ NTA < 58212 
... 
bin10: 261954 ≤ NTA 
CellSize = small: 
bin1: 0 ≤ NTA < 728 
bin2: 728 ≤ NTA < 1456 
... 
bin10: 6552 ≤ NTA

Reserved
